SECTIONED BUILD RULE (QUALITY CONTROL)

SECTIONED BUILD OVERRIDE (QUEUE RULE â€” CRITICAL)

When Mode 1 Sectioned Review Output is active:

â€¢ Any rule elsewhere that says â€œMUST generateâ€ a card type
  (e.g., syndrome high-yield pairs, mechanism requirements, traps, etc.)
  MUST be treated as a QUEUED REQUIREMENT.

Meaning:
â€¢ The assistant MUST NOT emit cards outside the currently active section.
â€¢ Instead, it must queue the requirement and generate it only when the workflow reaches that section.

Examples:
â€¢ If a syndrome is introduced during SECTION A (PRIMARY UNKNOWN),
  the required syndrome High-Yield pair MUST be generated later in:
  SECTION G (High-Yield), not immediately.

â€¢ If a mechanism is implied/required during SECTION A,
  it must be generated later in:
  SECTION D (Mechanism), not immediately.

â€¢ If a Boards Trap is implied during any section,
  it MUST be generated later in:
  SECTION E (Boards Trap), not immediately.

â€¢ If epidemiology pivots exist in the source,
  they MUST be generated later in:
  SECTION F (Epidemiology), not immediately.

This rule supersedes all â€œgenerate immediatelyâ€ language elsewhere.
Cards must be generated and reviewed in discrete sections.
Do NOT generate â€œeverything in one shot.â€

Section order is STRICT:

SECTION A) PRIMARY UNKNOWN cases
SECTION B) Differential Drills
SECTION C) Definition cards only
SECTION D) Mechanism cards
SECTION E) Boards Trap cards
SECTION F) Epidemiology cards (High-Yield pivots only; if present in source)
SECTION G) High-Yield (non-epid, non-definition; includes diagnostic performance + outcomes when present)

Before outputting SECTION A, the assistant MUST already have completed:
â€¢ Core Validation Gate requirements
â€¢ Whole-Source Coverage Audit requirements
â€¢ Core Summary requirements when Pathway A is active

SECTION A CASE LEDGER (MANDATORY BEFORE PREVIEW)

Immediately before the SECTION A Structured Card Preview, the assistant MUST output a PRIMARY UNKNOWN case ledger that accounts for every user-provided intended SECTION A case.

The ledger MUST include:
â€¢ Total user-provided cases: X
â€¢ Eligible for PRIMARY UNKNOWN: Y
â€¢ EXCLUDED from PRIMARY UNKNOWN: Z
â€¢ PRIMARY UNKNOWN cards generated in SECTION A: Y

Then list:
â€¢ every excluded case with its one-line reason

Then explicitly confirm:
â€¢ "SECTION A cardinality check passed: eligible case count matches PRIMARY UNKNOWN count."

Section A case accounting rules:
â€¢ every user-provided intended SECTION A case must be assigned a case index
â€¢ every indexed case must be marked ELIGIBLE or EXCLUDED
â€¢ every EXCLUDED case must carry a one-line allowed reason
â€¢ every ELIGIBLE case must map one-to-one to exactly one PRIMARY UNKNOWN note
â€¢ Section A deduplication is forbidden
â€¢ no eligible case may be merged, substituted, or silently deferred

If the counts do NOT match:
â€¢ STOP
â€¢ Output: "SECTION A blocked - eligible case count does not match PRIMARY UNKNOWN count."
â€¢ Then list the missing or extra case(s) by case index.
â€¢ Do NOT preview SECTION A.

For each section:
â€¢ Output ONLY that sectionâ€™s Structured Card Preview.
â€¢ Do NOT output other sections.
â€¢ Wait for user approval (explicit â€œapprovedâ€ or â€œnext sectionâ€) before proceeding, UNLESS an autonomous batch mode override is present.
â€¢ If an autonomous batch mode override is present:
  â†’ section previews are internal validation checkpoints
  â†’ do NOT pause for user approval between sections
  â†’ do NOT output user-facing section-by-section previews unless a hard stop or major repair explanation must be shown

Structured Card Preview rules remain:
â€¢ Do NOT display full summary text anywhere in Review mode.
â€¢ For any RadPrimer/STATdx-origin card: display ONLY the note: â€œSummary field included.â€

-----------------------------------------------------

SECTION-LEVEL COVERAGE ENFORCEMENT (MANDATORY)

Before outputting each section preview, the assistant MUST verify that all content from the Whole-Source Coverage Audit relevant to that section has been considered.

For each section, the assistant must internally check:

â€¢ Which Core-derived items belong in this section
â€¢ Which article-derived items belong in this section
â€¢ Which non-overlapping high-yield items must be included to preserve mastery
â€¢ Which items are intentionally deferred to later sections under the queue rule

No section may be generated from digest-only understanding.
No section may be generated from Core Summary alone.
No section may be generated from summary field text alone.

Mode 2 â€” TSV Output (STRICT FORMAT):

â€¢ No header row.
â€¢ Tabs only.
â€¢ One note per line.
â€¢ Column count MUST be exactly:
  22 columns total = 21 fields (core_rad_notetype) + final Tags column.
â€¢ Clinical_Context can NEVER be empty.
â€¢ The final Tags column MUST remain present and MUST be blank / empty for every exported row.
â€¢ If any earlier rule conceptually references tag categories or ontology labels, those references MUST NOT populate the final TSV Tags column.
â€¢ The final TSV Tags column is an intentionally empty placeholder in this workflow.

TSV Structural Integrity Rule (CRITICAL)

â€¢ No literal newline characters (\n or \r) are allowed inside any field.
â€¢ Every note must occupy exactly one physical line in the TSV file.
â€¢ All internal formatting must use <br> instead of newline characters.
â€¢ Any violation invalidates the TSV.

Summary HTML Rule (TSV)
â€¢ The `summary` field must render as simple Anki-safe HTML, not raw markdown.
â€¢ Allowed summary HTML should remain limited to simple tags such as:
  <b> <br> <div> <ul> <ol> <li>
â€¢ The same article-level summary content must be reused identically across all cards from the same article/case bundle.
â€¢ The `summary` field must not contain literal emoji or other non-ASCII icon characters.
â€¢ Any summary icon anchor must be encoded as an HTML numeric character reference, such as `&#x1F50D;`, so TSV text stays ASCII-safe and does not turn into question marks during clipboard/console handling.

PREVIEW â†’ TSV IDENTITY LOCK (CRITICAL)

2) The TSV MUST include:
   â€¢ Every HIGH-YIELD (including definition cards)
   â€¢ Every UNKNOWN
   â€¢ Every DIFFERENTIAL DRILL
   â€¢ Every MECHANISM

   â€¢ Add new cards
   â€¢ Remove cards

   â€¢ Substitute â€œexampleâ€ cards

   â€¢ Re-interpret architecture at export time

   except for minimal formatting adjustments needed to satisfy TSV rules
   (e.g., converting any accidental newlines to <br>).

   (canonical order + within-section sequence),
   unless the user explicitly requests a different ordering.

ACTIVE PREVIEW SET DEFINITION (SECTIONED)

â€¢ In standard manual mode:
  â†’ The â€œactive preview setâ€ is the most recent USER-APPROVED section preview.
  â†’ TSV export is allowed ONLY for sections that have been explicitly approved.
  â†’ If a section is modified after approval:
    â†’ that section must be re-previewed and re-approved before TSV export.

â€¢ If an autonomous batch mode override is present:
  â†’ The â€œactive preview setâ€ is the most recent internally validated section or full-deck snapshot that passed all automatic checks.
  â†’ TSV export is allowed ONLY for sections that have passed automatic validation.
  â†’ If a section is modified after repair:
    â†’ that section must be internally re-validated before TSV export.

COMPLETE PREVIEW REQUIREMENT (MANDATORY)

â€¢ Definition cards ONLY for high-yield source-emphasized definitions, diagnostic criteria, named syndrome definitions, or important boundary definitions

â€¢ TSV export is prohibited.

  â€œTSV export blocked â€” preview-to-TSV identity lock failed.â€

Pre-TSV Validation Gate (MUST PASS BEFORE TSV):

A) Trigger Integrity (Architecture Safety)
â€¢ UNKNOWN cards: Image MUST be populated AND Question MUST be populated.
â€¢ If Image is populated but Question is empty â†’ it must NOT be treated as UNKNOWN.
â€¢ Any non-UNKNOWN card that includes Image MUST keep Question empty.
â€¢ Differential Drill exists ONLY when Differentials is populated.
â€¢ Mechanism exists ONLY when Mechanism is populated.
â€¢ Boards Trap exists ONLY when Boards_Trap is populated.
â€¢ High-Yield exists ONLY when High_Yield_Q is populated.
â€¢ No unintended extra card types may be created by accidental field population.

A1) SECTION A PRIMARY UNKNOWN CARDINALITY (MANDATORY)
â€¢ Every user-provided intended SECTION A case MUST appear in the case inventory.
â€¢ Every inventoried case MUST be marked ELIGIBLE or EXCLUDED.
â€¢ Every EXCLUDED case MUST include a one-line allowed reason.
â€¢ Every ELIGIBLE case MUST map one-to-one to exactly one PRIMARY UNKNOWN note.
â€¢ No two eligible cases may share one PRIMARY UNKNOWN note.
â€¢ No eligible case may be omitted, merged, substituted, or silently deferred.
â€¢ Eligible case count MUST equal PRIMARY UNKNOWN count.

If any of the above fails:
â€¢ STOP
â€¢ Output: "TSV export blocked - SECTION A case ledger / PRIMARY UNKNOWN cardinality rule violated."
â€¢ Then list the missing, extra, or improperly excluded case(s) by case index.
â€¢ Do NOT output TSV.

B) Source Coverage + Non-Fabrication
â€¢ All board-relevant Core content for the topic is represented (without trivial duplication), unless Core GAP pathway is invoked.
â€¢ All board-relevant RadPrimer/STATdx content for the topic is represented (when provided).
â€¢ All high-value non-overlapping article content needed for durable mastery is represented when article-based generation is being used.
â€¢ Whole-Source Coverage Audit requirements were completed before section generation.
â€¢ If Pathway A was used, Core Summary requirements were completed before SECTION A.
â€¢ No fabricated:
  imaging findings
  MRI signal/sequence behavior
  ultrasound behavior (echogenicity, echotexture, posterior acoustic behavior, Doppler behavior, compressibility, mobility, wall layering, maneuver findings, or source-named sonographic signs/artifacts)
  differentials (EXCEPT explicitly labeled Model-inferred differentials permitted under CONTROLLED INFERENCE)
  epidemiology
  thresholds / staging / management triggers
â€¢ If anything is inferred (rare): it MUST be explicitly labeled:
  â€œNot explicitly listed in Core/RadPrimer/STATdx; inferred based on imaging pattern.â€

C) Image/Captions â†’ Keyword Findings Integrity (UNKNOWN ONLY)
â€¢ For UNKNOWN cards:
  Most_Likely_Diagnosis must include caption-derived KEYWORD FINDINGS (3â€“8 phrases typical)
  Those phrases must be explicitly present in the verbatim captions
  No inference beyond caption text
â€¢ Image_Annotated order must match Image order (when present).
â€¢ If a multi-image card has caption-supported time/procedure/phase differences, neutral context labels appear before the affected images, do not leak the answer, and do not alter verbatim captions.

D) Differential Drill De-duplication (Pattern-Based; Discriminator-Driven)

Core Principle:
Drill generation is determined by Dominant Imaging Pattern and Primary Discriminator Logic â€” NOT by exact differential list equality.

STEP 1 â€” Identify Dominant Pattern
â€¢ For each potential Differential Drill, explicitly classify the dominant imaging pattern.
â€¢ The dominant pattern is defined by the primary discriminator that separates the leading entities.
â€¢ Examples:
  - Calcified Encasing Peritoneum Pattern
  - Smooth Diffuse Enhancing Peritoneum Pattern
  - Gas-Containing Ascites Pattern
  - Solid Polypoid Mass Pattern
  - Circumferential Stricture Pattern
  - Post-Operative Leak Pattern

STEP 2 â€” Deduplication Rule
â€¢ If two cases share the SAME dominant pattern AND the SAME primary discriminator logic:
  â†’ Generate ONLY ONE Differential Drill.
  â†’ All other cases must leave Differentials blank.
  â†’ Discriminator reasoning may still appear in the associated UNKNOWN reasoning or in source-supported differentiation fields where permitted by architecture.

â€¢ If two cases differ in dominant pattern OR require a different primary discriminator strategy:
  â†’ A new Differential Drill is ALLOWED.
  â†’ Overlap in differential lists does NOT prevent generation.

STEP 3 â€” Inflation Suppression
Do NOT generate a new drill if:
â€¢ The same mental separation strategy would be repeated.
â€¢ The same dominant discriminator is being trained.
â€¢ Only minor list variation exists without a new cognitive pivot.

STEP 4 â€” Justification Requirement
If generating a new drill in a topic where another drill already exists,
Imaging_Differentiation MUST begin with:
â€œDominant pattern differs from other cases because: [distinct discriminator explanation].â€

This enforces conscious pattern separation and prevents silent duplication.

Key Rule:
Pattern distinctiveness overrides list variation.
Exact differential-set comparison is NOT the deduplication mechanism.

E) Differential Drill Structural Enforcement (CRITICAL)
Applies to every note where Differentials is populated:

Required Field Presence + Isolation
â€¢ Differential_Q MUST be populated.
â€¢ Imaging_Differentiation MUST be populated.
â€¢ Question MUST be blank.
â€¢ Mechanism_Q / Mechanism MUST be blank.
â€¢ Boards_Trap_Q / Boards_Trap MUST be blank.
â€¢ High_Yield_Q / High_Yield_A MUST be blank.

Mode Determination (MANDATORY)
â€¢ If a drill originates from an existing UNKNOWN case:
  â†’ This Differential Drill MUST be MODE 1 (case-bundled).
  â†’ Standalone mode is NOT allowed.
â€¢ If no such UNKNOWN exists:
  â†’ MODE 2 may be used (rare), but must satisfy Mode 2 rules below.

MODE 1 (Case-Bundled) Requirements
â€¢ Clinical_Context MUST preserve the same blinded clinical wording as the associated UNKNOWN card, but MUST be unique at the note level to prevent duplicate-note conflicts.
â€¢ A short deterministic suffix (e.g., [DD1]) is allowed and expected for case-bundled Differential Drills.
â€¢ Image MUST be populated and MUST match the associated UNKNOWN Image exactly.
â€¢ If the associated UNKNOWN card contains Image_Annotated (non-empty):
  â†’ The Differential Drill MUST include the exact same Image_Annotated block
    (same stackItem blocks + verbatim captions).
  â†’ Missing Image_Annotated in this scenario = structural failure.
â€¢ Entity_Label is RECOMMENDED and must contain diagnosis only (no descriptors/findings/reasoning).
â€¢ Most_Likely_Diagnosis must be blank OR diagnosis-only (single line). No keyword findings or reasoning.

MODE 2 (Standalone) Requirements (RARE)
â€¢ Clinical_Context MUST be a unique 12-character alphanumeric/symbolic ID and NOTHING else.
â€¢ Entity_Label is REQUIRED (diagnosis-only).
â€¢ Image is OPTIONAL.
â€¢ Most_Likely_Diagnosis must be blank OR diagnosis-only (single line).

Front-Side Blinding Audit (Differential Drill)
â€¢ Front may contain ONLY:
  Clinical_Context
  Differential_Q
  Image stack (if present)
â€¢ Front must NOT contain:
  diagnosis names (except neutral Entity_Label if template prints it)
  named differentials
  caption-derived keyword findings
  named signs
  management clues

=== FUSED MASTER SOURCE PACKAGE ===
# Acute Subdural Hematoma

Canonical hierarchy: All Categories > Basic > Neuroradiology > Brain > Primary Effects of CNS Trauma > Acute Subdural Hematoma
Canonical deck path: Corebook::Neuro::Brain::Primary Effects of CNS Trauma::Acute Subdural Hematoma
Primary source posture: RadPrimer supplies the canonical hierarchy/backbone; STATdx supplies supplemental depth and the default higher-resolution selected image set.
Core evidence: no auditable Core Radiology source was supplied in this bundle, so Core-specific support is not asserted.

## Source Coverage And Image Gate

STATdx fully covers the 10-image RadPrimer set with visually exact same-screenshot or same-graphic counterparts in the staged image_evidence files. The RadPrimer and STATdx binary hashes differ because the evidence exports use different source render sizes/compression levels, but direct visual inspection of the staged files shows the same screenshot/slice/graphic for every mapped pair. Therefore, the default teaching/download set uses STATdx images 1-25, while RadPrimer images 1-10 remain in the registry as archive-optional exact duplicates for audit traceability.

RadPrimer image 1 -> STATdx image 1: exact duplicate; mechanism graphic of acute SDH compressing the left hemisphere with associated contusions/axonal injuries.
RadPrimer image 2 -> STATdx image 2: exact duplicate; classic left convexity acute SDH with internal hypodense unclotted blood.
RadPrimer image 3 -> STATdx image 3: exact duplicate; paired standard/wide-window NECT comparison for subtle SDH and disproportionate swelling.
RadPrimer image 4 -> STATdx image 10: exact duplicate; isodense acute SDH in an anemic patient with inward gray-white displacement and midline shift.
RadPrimer image 5 -> STATdx image 5: exact duplicate; coronal graphic of thin falcine/tentorial acute SDH.
RadPrimer images 6-8 -> STATdx images 21-23: exact duplicate atomic same-patient peritentorial SDH multiplanar cluster.
RadPrimer images 9-10 -> STATdx images 24-25: exact duplicate atomic rapid-expansion time-lapse cluster.
No RadPrimer image is classified as near duplicate, conceptual replacement, or not covered.

## Fused Teaching Backbone

### Definition And Mechanism

- [Both] Acute subdural hematoma is acute blood in or between the inner border cell layer of the dura and the arachnoid.
- [Both] Trauma is the most common cause; the classic mechanism is tearing of bridging cortical veins as they cross the subdural space to drain into the dural sinuses.
- [Both] Older adults are especially vulnerable after minor trauma because cerebral atrophy permits greater cortical motion and bridging-vein strain.
- [STATdx] Nontraumatic/spontaneous causes include dissection of intraparenchymal hemorrhage into the subarachnoid/subdural space, aneurysm rupture, dural AVF/AVM/cavernoma, moyamoya, dural tumor invasion, severe coagulopathy, and cerebral amyloid angiopathy.
- [Both] More than 70% of acute SDH cases have other significant traumatic lesions; if mass effect or shift is greater than expected for hematoma thickness, suspect underlying edema/excitotoxic injury.

### Imaging Pattern

- [Both] Noncontrast CT is the initial screening study. Use bone and soft-tissue algorithms, standard brain windows, and wider windows around 150 HU when SDH is subtle or isodense.
- [Both] The typical CT finding is a crescentic hyperdense extraaxial collection that spreads diffusely over the affected convexity and may extend along the falx, tentorium, and anterior/middle cranial fossa floors.
- [Both] Acute SDH may cross sutures but does not cross dural attachments. It causes inward displacement of cortical veins, sulci, and the gray-white interface.
- [Both] Hyperacute SDH can be heterogeneous or hypodense. In the 6-hour to 3-day acute window, about 60% are homogeneously hyperdense and about 40% are mixed density due to active bleeding/swirl, CSF admixture from arachnoid tear, or clot retraction.
- [STATdx] STATdx explicitly frames CSF admixture as hematohygroma/arachnoid tear physiology; this is useful when an acute SDH has unexpectedly low-density components.
- [Both] Rare isodense acute SDH occurs with coagulopathy or severe anemia and is best detected by gray-white/cortical vein displacement and widened window settings.
- [Both] Coronal and sagittal reformats are best for small falcine, tentorial, or convexity components that are difficult on axial images alone.
- [Both] MR is more sensitive than CT but is rarely the initial trauma study; it better depicts extent, age variability, traumatic brain injury, and nontraumatic causes.

### MR And CTA Details

- [Both] Acute SDH signal is variable and can evolve like intraparenchymal hemorrhage, but recurrent bleeding and CSF dilution make exact age assignment difficult.
- [Both] On T1WI, hyperacute SDH is iso- to mildly hyperintense and acute SDH may be mildly hypointense; on T2WI, hyperacute SDH may be mildly hyperintense and acute SDH is often hypointense.
- [Both] FLAIR is often conspicuous because SDH is usually hyperintense to CSF, though acute collections can be isointense to CSF from T2-shortening effects.
- [Both] T2* GRE is usually hypointense unless the collection is hyperacute; DWI is nonspecific but helps distinguish empyema when central diffusion restriction is marked.
- [Both] CTA mainly demonstrates mass effect and displaced veins; DSA is reserved when CTA suggests aneurysm or dural vascular malformation.
- [STATdx] STATdx images add a CTA spot-sign/active extravasation teaching cluster: STATdx image 8 follows the heterogeneous SDH in STATdx image 7, and STATdx image 9 shows the 24-hour enlargement before decompression.

### Differential Diagnosis

- [Both] Other subdural collections include mixed acute-on-chronic/subacute SDH, hygroma, effusion, and empyema.
- [Both] Hygroma is clear CSF from torn arachnoid, often after surgery or trauma; effusion is near-CSF-density xanthochromic fluid from membrane/plasma extravasation or meningitis.
- [Both] Subdural empyema shows peripheral enhancement, FLAIR hyperintensity, and restricted diffusion on DWI.
- [Both] Acute epidural hematoma is typically biconvex, strongly fracture-associated, limited by sutures, and may cross dural attachments; acute SDH is usually crescentic and can cross sutures.
- [Both] Pachymeningopathies, dural tumors, and chemical shift artifact can mimic subdural pathology in the right setting.
- [STATdx] Skull metastases may result in acute SDH, so bone windows should be reviewed when the context is atypical or nontraumatic.

### Clinical Course And Management

- [Both] Presentation ranges from asymptomatic to loss of consciousness. A lucid interval can occur when an initially alert patient deteriorates hours after trauma.
- [Both] Advanced age, early symptoms within 4 hours, anticoagulation, and coagulopathy increase risk and worsen prognosis.
- [Both] Acute SDH can grow with increasing mass effect if untreated. Recurrent hemorrhage is common; in children, recurrent or mixed-age hemorrhage should raise concern for nonaccidental trauma.
- [Both] Thin isolated falcotentorial acute SDH, around 3 mm or less, in a young patient with GCS 13-15 typically does not enlarge and may not need repeat head CT.
- [Both] Surgically relevant features include maximum hematoma thickness of 10 mm or greater, midline shift, and clinical deterioration.
- [Both] Mortality is high, and hematoma volume greater than 8-10% of intracranial volume is lethal. Emergency preoperative high-dose mannitol may improve outcome in selected surgical cases.
- [STATdx] STATdx supplemental captions emphasize that severe mass effect, edema, subfalcine/transtentorial herniation, obstructed foramen of Monro, and temporal horn displacement are poor-prognosis findings.

Use the following primary images by default. RadPrimer counterparts are retained only as archive-optional duplicate evidence.

- STATdx image 1: mechanism graphic for acute SDH compressing the hemisphere with associated contusions and axonal injuries.
- STATdx image 2: classic axial NECT left convexity acute SDH with unclotted low-density foci and mass effect.
- STATdx image 3: standard versus wide-window comparison showing a subtle SDH and disproportionate cortical swelling.
- STATdx image 4: axial T1 MR showing a left convexity acute SDH at 24 hours and subfalcine herniation.
- STATdx image 5: coronal graphic of thin falcine and tentorial acute SDH.
- STATdx image 6: coronal NECT falcine/tentorial SDH variant with scalp hematoma, useful for management nuance that these often do not need surgery.
- STATdx images 7-9: atomic active-bleeding cluster: heterogeneous acute SDH after fall, follow-up CTA spot sign, and 24-hour enlargement before decompression.
- STATdx image 10: isodense acute SDH in an anemic patient with gray-white interface displacement and midline shift.
- STATdx image 11: classic crescentic hyperdense extraaxial collection with compression and displacement of the brain.
- STATdx images 12-15: atomic subtle tentorial cluster with axial, coronal, sagittal left tentorial, and right-sided normal-dura comparison views.
- STATdx images 16-18: atomic severe herniation cluster in an anticoagulated obtunded patient, including obstructed foramen of Monro and fatal coronal herniation pattern.
- STATdx images 19-20: atomic MR signal cluster showing acute right SDH on T1 and T2 with a chronic contralateral SDH for contrast.
- STATdx images 21-23: atomic peritentorial same-patient multiplanar cluster, replacing RadPrimer images 6-8.
- STATdx images 24-25: atomic rapid-expansion time-lapse cluster, replacing RadPrimer images 9-10.

- Treat archive-optional RadPrimer images as audit/completeness records, not as default card or lecture images.
